Output only the translation. <NL> English: And that is actually for the last 500 years, since its very successful introduction, I must say. <NL> Spanish:	 Y esto ha sido realmente durante los últimos 500 años, desde su muy exitosa introducción, tengo que decirlo. <NL>  <NL> Here's the reasoning behind this translation: <NL> 1. The English sentence refers to something that has been happening in the past until the present, which is reflected in the use of "has been" tense. In Spanish, the -ando/-iendo form is used for this tense, so "ha sido" is appropriate here. <NL> 2. "For the last 500 years" translates to "durante los últimos 500 años" in Spanish, which maintains the sense of a duration extending up to the present moment. <NL> 3. The sentence mentions that the event has been successful since its introduction, indicated by "its very successful introduction." In Spanish, "su muy exitosa introducción" captures this meaning. <NL> 4. To maintain a formal tone, "tengo que decirlo" (I must say) is added to convey the speaker's evaluation of the event as a very successful one.
